width:4.081ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> is hence independent of the frame in which it is measured. \n</p><p>In considering the physical significance of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta s^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta s^{2}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Delta s^{2}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5d76e6fc5f1353a997222afbf3f50f1e57731a17" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:4.081ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>, there are three cases to note:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morin2007_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-Morin2007-25">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor1966_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor1966-45">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>25&#8211;39</span></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>&#916;s<sup>2</sup> &gt; 0:</b> In this case, the two events are separated by more time than space, and they are hence said to be <i>timelike</i> separated. This implies that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle |\\Delta x/\\Delta t|&lt;c,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&lt;</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle |\\Delta x/\\Delta t|&lt;c,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle |\\Delta x/\\Delta t|&lt;c,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f7bd0cb9f549ff0e71686c8d03731a00c803cb5d" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.249ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> and given the Lorentz transformation <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta x\'=\\gamma \\ (\\Delta x-v\\,\\Delta t),}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta x\'=\\gamma \\ (\\Delta x-v\\,\\Delta t),}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Delta x\'=\\gamma \\ (\\Delta x-v\\,\\Delta t),}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/08638dcd8661addff0d34eeba30764812364ef85" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:21.744ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> it is evident that there exists a <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.128ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> less than <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> for which <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta x\'=0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta x\'=0}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Delta x\'=0}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/13efc239af4739c8857438b3aebf273a2edd4266" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:8.211ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> (in particular, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v=\\Delta x/\\Delta t}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v=\\Delta x/\\Delta t}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle v=\\Delta x/\\Delta t}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6dced72fdf712754acc3ee84c950f882909bdb4a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.43ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>). In other words, given two events that are timelike separated, it is possible to find a frame in which the two events happen at the same place. In this frame, the separation in time, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta s/c,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta s/c,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Delta s/c,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9ec3659a31fde67e04a729967a7ee194cd20562f" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:5.842ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is called the <i>proper time</i>.</li>\n<li><b>&#916;s<sup>2</sup> &lt; 0:</b> In this case, the two events are separated by more space than time, and they are hence said to be <i>spacelike</i> separated. This implies that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle |\\Delta x/\\Delta t|&gt;c,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&gt;</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle |\\Delta x/\\Delta t|&gt;c,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle |\\Delta x/\\Delta t|&gt;c,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f7b6aecb68fea0b12ce1463664a64391f0b3fd68" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.249ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> and given the Lorentz transformation <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=\\gamma \\ (\\Delta t-v\\Delta x/c^{2}),}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=\\gamma \\ (\\Delta t-v\\Delta x/c^{2}),}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=\\gamma \\ (\\Delta t-v\\Delta x/c^{2}),}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8e6abf75d79c46d70385523235463b495d6ae145" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:24.09ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> there exists a <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.128ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> less than <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> for which  <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=0}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=0}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/79312af2caef81493091b785626154e3b97c172c" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.721ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>  (in particular, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v=c^{2}\\Delta t/\\Delta x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v=c^{2}\\Delta t/\\Delta x}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle v=c^{2}\\Delta t/\\Delta x}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a3e18d875265386f590cf5016a44358c43590d3c" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.491ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span>). In other words, given two events that are spacelike separated, it is possible to find a frame in which the two events happen at the same time. In this frame, the separation in space, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {-\\Delta s^{2}}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {-\\Delta s^{2}}},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {-\\Delta s^{2}}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9862c1316d2ea79f297378b685193479b6c37f13" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.859ex; height:3.509ex;"/></span> is called the <i>proper distance</i>, or <i>proper length</i>. For values of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.128ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> greater than and less than <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c^{2}\\Delta t/\\Delta x,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c^{2}\\Delta t/\\Delta x,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle c^{2}\\Delta t/\\Delta x,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9a5f1f8fedab7da0563ac0e47c7f6d14f4e0f8b6" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.911ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> the sign of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\Delta t\'" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/50ea24905e052383d75e10e87e33a3d805d39b43" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.46ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> changes, meaning that the temporal order of spacelike-separated events changes depending on the frame in which the events are viewed. The temporal order of timelike-separated events, however, is absolute, since the only way that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.128ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> could be greater than  <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c^{2}\\Delta t/\\Delta x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c^{2}\\Delta t/\\Delta x}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle c^{2}\\Delta t/\\Delta x}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d0f9edf99cb4c2d855f683f5d86ce5a21d01930c" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.265ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> would be if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v&gt;c.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>&gt;</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v&gt;c.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle v&gt;c.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4b1b37eb8784e59971c610cb92e0326707f96044" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.88ex; height:1.843ex;"/></span></li>\n<li><b>&#916;s<sup>2</sup> = 0:</b> In this case, the two events are said to be <i>lightlike</i> separated. This implies that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle |\\Delta x/\\Delta t|=c,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle |\\Delta x/\\Delta t|=c,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle |\\Delta x/\\Delta t|=c,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/76ec5196dbc4bda6dba50dac636b136864529116" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.249ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> and this relationship is frame independent due to the invariance of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle s^{2}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s^{2}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle s^{2}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/54d50a9d7ee6af438d38a27aa3faf9e3cd0560ea" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.792ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> From this, we observe that the speed of light is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> in every inertial frame. In other words, starting from the assumption of universal Lorentz covariance, the constant speed of light is a derived result, rather than a postulate as in the two-postulates formulation of the special theory.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relativity_of_simultaneity">Relativity of simultaneity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_relativity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Relativity of simultaneity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Relativity_of_simultaneity" title="Relativity of simultaneity">Relativity of simultaneity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ladder_paradox" title="Ladder paradox">Ladder paradox</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Relativity_of_Simultaneity_Animation.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Relativity_of_Simultaneity_Animation.gif/220px-Relativity_of_Simultaneity_Animation.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Relativity_of_Simultaneity_Animation.gif/330px-Relativity_of_Simultaneity_Animation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/78/Relativity_of_Simultaneity_Animation.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Relativity_of_Simultaneity_Animation.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure 4-1. The three events (A, B, C) are simultaneous in the reference frame of some observer <b>O</b>. In a reference frame moving at <i>v</i> = 0.3<i>c</i>, as measured by <b>O</b>, the events occur in the order C, B, A. In a reference frame moving at <i>v</i> = -0.5<i>c</i> with respect to  <b>O</b>, the events occur in the order A, B, C. The white lines, the <i>lines of simultaneity</i>, move from the past to the future in the respective frames (green coordinate axes), highlighting events residing on it. They are the locus of all events occurring at the same time in the respective frame. The gray area is the light cone with respect to the origin of all considered frames.</div></div></div>\n<p>Two events happening in two different locations that occur simultaneously in the reference frame of one inertial observer, may occur non-simultaneously in the reference frame of another inertial observer (lack of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absolute_simultaneity" title="Absolute simultaneity">absolute simultaneity</a>).\n</p><p>From <b><a href="#math_3">Equation&#160;3</a></b> (the forward Lorentz transformation in terms of coordinate differences)\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=\\gamma \\left(\\Delta t-{\\frac {v\\,\\Delta x}{c^{2}}}\\right)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=\\gamma \\left(\\Delta t-{\\frac {v\\,\\Delta x}{c^{2}}}\\right)}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\Delta t\' = \\gamma \\left(\\Delta t - \\frac{v \\,\\Delta x}{c^{2}} \\right)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ac5082c4895196aa92bc26edc9bb606b7669fb1f" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:22.862ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>it is clear that two events that are simultaneous in frame <i>S</i> (satisfying <span class="nowrap">&#916;<i>t</i> = 0</span>), are not necessarily simultaneous in another inertial frame <i>S</i>&#8242; (satisfying <span class="nowrap">&#916;<i>t</i>&#8242; = 0</span>). Only if these events are additionally co-local in frame <i>S</i> (satisfying <span class="nowrap">&#916;<i>x</i> = 0</span>), will they be simultaneous in another frame <i>S</i>&#8242;.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sagnac_effect" title="Sagnac effect">Sagnac effect</a> can be considered a manifestation of the relativity of simultaneity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ashby2003_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ashby2003-46">[26]</a></sup> Since relativity of simultaneity is a first order effect in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.128ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morin2007_25-5"><a href="#cite_note-Morin2007-25">[15]</a></sup> instruments based on the Sagnac effect for their operation, such as <a href="/wiki/Ring_laser_gyroscope" title="Ring laser gyroscope">ring laser gyroscopes</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiber_optic_gyroscope" title="Fiber optic gyroscope">fiber optic gyroscopes</a>, are capable of extreme levels of sensitivity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lin1979_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lin1979-47">[p 14]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Time_dilation">Time dilation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_relativity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Time dilation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Time_dilation" title="Time dilation">Time dilation</a></div>\n<p>The time lapse between two events is not invariant from one observer to another, but is dependent on the relative speeds of the observers\' reference frames (e.g., the <a href="/wiki/Twin_paradox" title="Twin paradox">twin paradox</a> which concerns a twin who flies off in a spaceship traveling near the speed of light and returns to discover that the non-traveling twin sibling has aged much more). \n</p><p>Suppose a <a href="/wiki/Clock" title="Clock">clock</a> is at rest in the unprimed system <i>S</i>. The location of the clock on two different ticks is then characterized by <span class="nowrap">&#916;<i>x</i> = 0</span>. To find the relation between the times between these ticks as measured in both systems, <b><a href="#math_3">Equation&#160;3</a></b> can be used to find:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=\\gamma \\,\\Delta t}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=\\gamma \\,\\Delta t}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\Delta t\' = \\gamma\\, \\Delta t " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/97f216b0be7c75fbdddecc96761aa6bb08ec6f03" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.984ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;for events satisfying&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta x=0\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta x=0\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\Delta x = 0 \\ ." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5fcaea5f99fa8bf00b7aff6f5a919e63d085a97a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:8.754ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>This shows that the time (&#916;<i>t</i>&#8242;) between the two ticks as seen in the frame in which the clock is moving (<i>S</i>&#8242;), is <i>longer</i> than the time (&#916;<i>t</i>) between these ticks as measured in the rest frame of the clock (<i>S</i>). Time dilation explains a number of physical phenomena; for example, the lifetime of high speed <a href="/wiki/Muon" title="Muon">muons</a> created by the collision of cosmic rays with particles in the Earth\'s outer atmosphere and moving towards the surface is greater than the lifetime of slowly moving muons, created and decaying in a laboratory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[27]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Length_contraction">Length contraction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_relativity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Length contraction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lorentz_contraction" title="Lorentz contraction">Lorentz contraction</a></div>\n<p>The dimensions (e.g., length) of an object as measured by one observer may be smaller than the results of measurements of the same object made by another observer (e.g., the <a href="/wiki/Ladder_paradox" title="Ladder paradox">ladder paradox</a> involves a long ladder traveling near the speed of light and being contained within a smaller garage).\n</p><p>Similarly, suppose a <a href="/wiki/Measuring_rod" title="Measuring rod">measuring rod</a> is at rest and aligned along the <i>x</i>-axis in the unprimed system <i>S</i>. In this system, the length of this rod is written as &#916;<i>x</i>. To measure the length of this rod in the system <i>S</i>&#8242;, in which the rod is moving, the distances <i>x</i>&#8242; to the end points of the rod must be measured simultaneously in that system <i>S</i>&#8242;. In other words, the measurement is characterized by <span class="nowrap">&#916;<i>t</i>&#8242; = 0</span>, which can be combined with <b><a href="#math_3">Equation&#160;3</a></b> to find the relation between the lengths &#916;<i>x</i> and &#916;<i>x</i>&#8242;:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta x\'={\\frac {\\Delta x}{\\gamma }}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta x\'={\\frac {\\Delta x}{\\gamma }}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\Delta x\' = \\frac{\\Delta x}{\\gamma} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8187d1893fb6b7efb0d681c4b47531b4707341e1" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:11.15ex; height:5.843ex;"/></span>&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;for events satisfying&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=0\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta t\'=0\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\Delta t\' = 0 \\ ." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e0826d5835ba3c1661c6d5d607755e074ab01d85" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:8.949ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>This shows that the length (&#916;<i>x</i>&#8242;) of the rod as measured in the frame in which it is moving (<i>S</i>&#8242;), is <i>shorter</i> than its length (&#916;<i>x</i>) in its own rest frame (<i>S</i>).\n</p><p>Time dilation and length contraction are not merely appearances. Time dilation is explicitly related to our way of measuring <i>time intervals</i> between events which occur at the same place in a given coordinate system (called "co-local" events). These time intervals will be <i>different</i> in another coordinate system moving with respect to the first, unless the events, in addition to being co-local, are also simultaneous. Similarly, length contraction relates to our measured distances between separated but simultaneous events in a given coordinate system of choice. If these events are not co-local, but are separated by distance (space), they will <i>not</i> occur at the same <i>spatial distance</i> from each other when seen from another moving coordinate system.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lorentz_transformation_of_velocities">Lorentz transformation of velocities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_relativity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Lorentz transformation of velocities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Velocity-addition_formula" title="Velocity-addition formula">Velocity-addition formula</a></div>\n<p>Consider two frames <i>S</i> and <i>S&#8242; </i> in standard configuration. A particle in <i>S</i> moves in the x direction with velocity vector <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u} .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u} .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\mathbf  {u}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b47f6c879cf8429300a0a2bb241649de2876ad2f" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.132ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> What is its velocity <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u\'} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msup>\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u\'} }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u\'} }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1517e7ccf782a3519acbc06b4b883a840b4d0459" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.17ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> in frame <i>S&#8242; </i>? \n</p><p>We can write\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="reference nourlexpansion" id="math_7" style="font-weight:bold; font-style:italic;">Eq. 7:</span> &#160;&#160; width:1.485ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> of the two velocities <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {v} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {v} }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mathbf {v} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/35c1866e359fbfd2e0f606c725ba5cc37a5195d6" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.411ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u\'} ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msup>\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u\'} ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u\'} ,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ba61bd1bf8a2ef484219bd3ffecca9ad5cca2938" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.817ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> and they replace the formula <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u=u\'+v} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n<mo mathvariant="bold">=</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo mathvariant="bold">+</mo>\n<mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u=u\'+v} }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u=u\'+v} }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9160bf66391ca30a404c05c7cd565fd2f4151fbb" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:11.544ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> which is valid in Galilean relativity. Interpreted in such a fashion, they are commonly referred to as the <i>relativistic velocity addition (or composition) formulas</i>, valid for the three axes of <i>S</i> and <i>S&#8242; </i> being aligned with each other (although not necessarily in standard configuration).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rindler0_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rindler0-14">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>47-49</span></sup>\n</p><p>We note the following points:\n</p>\n<ul><li>If an object (a <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">photon</a>) were moving at the speed of light in one frame <span class="nowrap">(i.e. <i>u</i> = &#177;<i>c</i></span> <span class="nowrap">or <i>u&#8242;</i> = &#177;<i>c</i>),</span> then it would also be moving at the speed of light in any other frame, moving at <span class="nowrap">|<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em;"><i>v</i></span>| &lt; <i>c</i></span>.</li>\n<li>The resultant speed of two velocities with magnitude less than <i>c</i> is always a velocity with magnitude less than <i>c</i>.</li>\n<li>If both |<i>u</i>| and |<i>v</i>| (and then also |<i>u&#8242;</i>| and |<i>v&#8242;</i>|) are small with respect to the speed of light (that is, <span class="nowrap">e.g., |<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em;"><span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;"><span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;"><i>u</i></span><span class="visualhide">/</span><span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;"><i>c</i></span></span></span>| &#8810; <span class="texhtml">1</span>),</span> then the intuitive Galilean transformations are recovered from the transformation equations for special relativity</li>\n<li>Attaching a frame to a photon (<i>riding a light beam</i> like Einstein) requires special treatment of the transformations.</li></ul>\n<p>There is nothing special about the <i>x</i> direction in the standard configuration. The above formalism applies to any direction; and three orthogonal directions allow dealing with all directions in space by decomposing the velocity vectors to their components in these directions. See <a href="/wiki/Velocity-addition_formula" title="Velocity-addition formula">Velocity-addition formula</a> for details.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thomas_rotation">Thomas rotation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_relativity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Thomas rotation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_rotation" title="Thomas rotation">Thomas rotation</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_1.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="213" data-file-width="485" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_1.svg/220px-Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_1.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_1.svg/330px-Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_1.svg/440px-Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_1.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_2.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="213" data-file-width="485" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_2.svg/220px-Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_2.svg/330px-Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_2.svg/440px-Thomas-Wigner_Rotation_2.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a></div></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Figure 4-2. Thomas-Wigner rotation</div></div></div>\n<p>The composition of two non-collinear Lorentz boosts (i.e. two non-collinear Lorentz transformations, neither of which involve rotation) results in a Lorentz transformation that is not a pure boost but is the composition of a boost and a rotation. \n</p><p>Thomas rotation results from the relativity of simultaneity. In Fig.&#160;4&#8209;2a, a rod of length <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle L}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/103168b86f781fe6e9a4a87b8ea1cebe0ad4ede8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.583ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> in its rest frame (i.e. having a <a href="/wiki/Proper_length" title="Proper length">proper length</a> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle L}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/103168b86f781fe6e9a4a87b8ea1cebe0ad4ede8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.583ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>) rises vertically along the y&#8209;axis in the ground frame. \n</p><p>In Fig.&#160;4&#8209;2b, the same rod is observed from the frame of a rocket moving at speed <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.128ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> to the right. If we imagine two clocks situated at the left and right ends of the rod that are synchronized <i>in the frame of the rod,</i> relativity of simultaneity causes the observer in the rocket frame to observe (not <a href="#Measurement_versus_visual_appearance"><i>see</i></a>) the clock at the right end of the rod as being advanced in time by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle Lv/c^{2},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle Lv/c^{2},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle Lv/c^{2},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/47f4f1edf4cc869335144bae1b6822e09cc75cb6" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.581ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> and the rod is correspondingly observed as tilted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor1966_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor1966-45">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>98&#8211;99</span></sup>\n</p><p>Unlike second-order relativistic effects such as length contraction or time dilation, this effect becomes quite significant even at fairly low velocities. For example, this can be seen in the <a href="/wiki/Spin%E2%80%93orbit_interaction" title="Spin&#8211;orbit interaction">spin of moving particles</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Thomas_precession" title="Thomas precession">Thomas precession</a> is a relativistic correction that applies to the <a href="/wiki/Spin_(physics)" title="Spin (physics)">spin</a> of an elementary particle or the rotation of a macroscopic <a href="/wiki/Gyroscope" title="Gyroscope">gyroscope</a>, relating the <a href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular velocity">angular velocity</a> of the spin of a particle following a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curvilinear" title="Curvilinear">curvilinear</a> orbit to the angular velocity of the orbital motion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor1966_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor1966-45">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>169&#8211;174</span></sup>\n</p><p>Thomas rotation provides the resolution to the well-known "meter stick and hole paradox".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shaw_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shaw-49">[p 15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor1966_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor1966-45">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>98&#8211;99</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Causality_and_prohibition_of_motion_faster_than_light">Causality and prohibition of motion faster than light</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_relativity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Causality and prohibition of motion faster than light">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Causality_(physics)" title="Causality (physics)">Causality (physics)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tachyonic_antitelephone" title="Tachyonic antitelephone">Tachyonic antitelephone</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Simple_light_cone_diagram.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="306" data-file-width="306" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Simple_light_cone_diagram.svg/220px-Simple_light_cone_diagram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Simple_light_cone_diagram.svg/330px-Simple_light_cone_diagram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Simple_light_cone_diagram.svg/440px-Simple_light_cone_diagram.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Simple_light_cone_diagram.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure 4-3. Light cone</div></div></div><p>In Fig.&#160;4&#8209;3, the interval between the events A and B is \'time-like\'; i.e., there is a frame of reference in which events A and B occur at the <i>same location in space</i>, separated only by occurring at different times. If A precedes B in that frame, then A precedes B in all frames accessible by a Lorentz transformation. It is possible for matter (or information) to travel (below light speed) from the location of A, starting at the time of A, to the location of B, arriving at the time of B, so there can be a causal relationship (with A the cause and B the effect).\n</p><p>The interval AC in the diagram is \'space-like\'; i.e., there is a frame of reference in which events A and C occur simultaneously, separated only in space. There are also frames in which A precedes C (as shown) and frames in which C precedes A. However, there are no frames accessible by a Lorentz transformation, in which events A and C occur at the same location. If it were possible for a cause-and-effect relationship to exist between events A and C, then paradoxes of causality would result.\n</p><p>For example, if signals could be sent faster than light, then signals could be sent into the sender\'s past (observer B in the diagrams).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[p 16]</a></sup> A variety of causal paradoxes could then be constructed. \n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:331px;max-width:331px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;margin-right:4px;width:162px;max-width:162px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Causality_violation_1.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="390" data-file-width="378" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Causality_violation_1.svg/160px-Causality_violation_1.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Causality_violation_1.svg/240px-Causality_violation_1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Causality_violation_1.svg/320px-Causality_violation_1.svg.png 2x" width="160"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Causality_violation_2.svg"><img alt="Three small white and yellow flowers before green-leaf background" data-file-height="390" data-file-width="378" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Causality_violation_2.svg/160px-Causality_violation_2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Causality_violation_2.svg/240px-Causality_violation_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Causality_violation_2.svg/320px-Causality_violation_2.svg.png 2x" width="160"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Figure 4-4. Causality violation by the use of fictitious<br/>"instantaneous communicators"</div></div></div>\n<p>Consider the spacetime diagrams in Fig.&#160;4&#8209;4. A and B stand alongside a railroad track, when a high speed train passes by, with C riding in the last car of the train and D riding in the leading car. The world lines of A and B are vertical (<i>ct</i>), distinguishing the stationary position of these observers on the ground, while the world lines of C and D are tilted forwards (<i>ct&#8242;</i>), reflecting the rapid motion of the observers C and D stationary in their train, as observed from the ground.\n</p>\n<ol><li>Fig.&#160;4&#8209;4a. The event of "B passing a message to D", as the leading car passes by, is at the origin of D\'s frame. D sends the message along the train to C in the rear car, using a fictitious "instantaneous communicator". The worldline of this message is the fat red arrow along the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle -x\'}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle -x\'}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="-x\'" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/48546807c94ca901131ea91fb0b2e64646d2d8d6" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:3.823ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> axis, which is a line of simultaneity in the primed frames of C and D. In the (unprimed) ground frame the signal arrives <i>earlier</i> than it was sent.</li>\n<li>Fig.&#160;4&#8209;4b. The event of "C passing the message to A", who is standing by the railroad tracks, is at the origin of their frames. Now A sends the message along the tracks to B via an "instantaneous communicator". The worldline of this message is the blue fat arrow, along the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle +x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle +x}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle +x}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2112b13188089a9983fb5b92fd192b21772d0dcc" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:3.138ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> axis, which is a line of simultaneity for the frames of A and B.</li></ol>\n<p>As seen from the spacetime diagram, B will receive the message before having sent it out, a violation of causality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Takeuchi_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Takeuchi-52">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is not necessary for signals to be instantaneous to violate causality. Even if the signal from D to C were slightly shallower than the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle x\'}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle x\'}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="x\'" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0ac74959896052e160a5953102e4bc3850fe93b2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.014ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> axis (and the signal from A to B slightly steeper than the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle x}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> axis), it would still be possible for B to receive his message before he had sent it. By increasing the speed of the train to near light speeds, the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle ct\'}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle ct\'}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle ct\'}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/23969b00bf6d4ac97e6b4058b9af2eb87ee3bf96" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.531ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle x\'}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle x\'}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="x\'" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0ac74959896052e160a5953102e4bc3850fe93b2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.014ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> axes can be squeezed very close to the dashed line representing the speed of light. With this modified setup, it can be demonstrated that even signals only <i>slightly</i> faster than the speed of light will result in causality violation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morin2017_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morin2017-53">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Therefore, if <a href="/wiki/Causality" title="Causality">causality</a> is to be preserved, one of the consequences of special relativity is that no information signal or material object can travel <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faster_than_light" title="Faster than light">faster than light</a> in vacuum. \n</p><p>This is not to say that <i>all</i> faster than light speeds are impossible. Various trivial situations can be described where some "things" move faster than light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[31]</a></sup> For example, the location where the beam of a search light hits the bottom of a cloud can move faster than light when the search light is turned rapidly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[33]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Optical_effects">Optical effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_relativity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Optical effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dragging_effects">Dragging effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special_relativity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Dragging effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fizeau_experiment" title="Fizeau experiment">Fizeau experiment</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fizeau_experiment_schematic.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="815" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Fizeau_experiment_schematic.svg/300px-Fizeau_experiment_schematic.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Fizeau_experiment_schematic.svg/450px-Fizeau_experiment_schematic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Fizeau_experiment_schematic.svg/600px-Fizeau_experiment_schematic.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fizeau_experiment_schematic.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure 5-1. Highly simplified diagram of Fizeau\'s 1851 experiment.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1850, <a href="/wiki/Hippolyte_Fizeau" title="Hippolyte Fizeau">Hippolyte Fizeau</a> and <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Foucault" title="L&#233;on Foucault">L&#233;on Foucault</a> independently established that light travels more slowly in water than in air, thus validating a prediction of <a href="/wiki/Augustin-Jean_Fresnel" title="Augustin-Jean Fresnel">Fresnel\'s</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wave_theory_of_light" title="Wave theory of light">wave theory of light</a> and invalidating the corresponding prediction of Newton\'s <a href="/wiki/Corpuscular_theory_of_light" title="Corpuscular theory of light">corpuscular theory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lauginie2004_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lauginie2004-57">[34]</a></sup> The speed of light was measured in still water. What would be the speed of light in flowing water?\n</p><p>In 1851, Fizeau conducted an experiment to answer this question, a simplified representation of which is illustrated in Fig.&#160;5&#8209;1. A beam of light is divided by a beam splitter, and the split beams are passed in opposite directions through a tube of flowing water. They are recombined to form interference fringes that an observer can view. Dragging of the light by the flowing water causes displacement of the fringes.\n</p><p>According to the theories prevailing at the time, light traveling through a moving medium would be a simple sum of its speed <i>through</i> the medium plus the speed <i>of</i> the medium. Contrary to expectation, Fizeau found that although light appeared to be dragged by the water, the magnitude of the dragging was much lower than expected. If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle u\'=c/n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>u</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>n</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle u\'=c/n}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle u\'=c/n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/58b3d46bcc8e549a628d05451b79b566b35b386a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.677ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> is the speed of light in still water, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.128ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is the speed of the water, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle u_{\\pm }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>u</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#177;<!-- &#177; --></mo>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle u_{\\pm }}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle u_{\\pm }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a4b35ae55d98b0339fccf145688295eef24812dc" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.84ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the water-bourne speed of light in the lab frame with the flow of water adding to or subtracting from the speed of light, then\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle u_{\\pm }={\\frac {c}{n}}\\pm v\\left(1-{\\frac {1}{n^{2}}}\\right)\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>u</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#177;<!-- &#177; --></mo>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mi>n</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#177;<!-- &#177; --></mo>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<msup>\n<mi>n</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle u_{\\pm }={\\frac {c}{n}}\\pm v\\left(1-{\\frac {1}{n^{2}}}\\right)\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle u_{\\pm }={\\frac {c}{n}}\\pm v\\left(1-{\\frac {1}{n^{2}}}\\right)\\ .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/600c359886ff9335f50b778121b56c2c1577af9f" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:24.849ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Fizeau\'s results, although consistent with Fresnel\'s earlier hypothesis of <a href="/wiki/Aether_drag_hypothesis" title="Aether drag hypothesis">partial aether dragging</a>, were extremely disconcerting to physicists of the time. Among other things, the presence of an index of refraction term meant that, since <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>n</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle n}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.395ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> depends on wavelength, <i>the aether must be capable of sustaining different motions at the same time.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[note 8]</a></sup> A variety of theoretical explanations were proposed to explain Fresnel\'s dragging coefficient that were completely at odds with each other. Even before the <a href="/wiki/Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment" title="Michelson&#8211;Morley experiment">Michelson&#8211;Morley experiment</a>, Fizeau\'s experimental results were among a number of observations that created a critical situation in explaining the optics of moving bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stachel2005_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stachel2005-61">[35]</a></sup>\n</p><p>From the point of view of special relativity, Fizeau\'s result is nothing but an approximation to <b><a href="#math_10">Equation&#160;10</a></b>, the relativistic formula for composition of velocities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rindler1977_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rindler1977-44">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle u_{\\pm }={\\frac {u\'\\pm v}{1\\pm u\'v/c^{2}}}=}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>u</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#177;<!-- &#177; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>u</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle u_{\\pm }={\\frac {u\'\\pm v}{1\\pm u\'v/c^{2}}}=}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle u_{\\pm }={\\frac {u\'\\pm v}{1\\pm u\'v/c^{2}}}=}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/223e20e02edd4e5f50666b06d1845b5309ca45aa" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:19.597ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {c/n\\pm v}{1\\pm v/cn}}\\approx }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>n</mi>\n<mo>&#177;<!-- &#177; width:11.984ex; height:6.509ex;"/></span> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c\\left({\\frac {1}{n}}\\pm {\\frac {v}{c}}\\right)\\left(1\\mp {\\frac {v}{cn}}\\right)\\approx }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mi>n</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#177;<!-- &#177;
